It is a single-purpose OTP relay, not an email system.\n\nWhat exists: one trait method, `send_otp` (`email/src/lib.rs:69`), with a live `LettreSmtpSender` (STARTTLS via OCI Email Delivery, rustls) and a `StubEmailSender` that logs the code in dev. Config is validated (`SmtpEmailConfig::validate`). It is wired into exactly **one** caller — open self-service signup. Admin-issued and credential-reset OTPs are returned **once in the API response** (`auth-rest` `OtpIssueResponse`), shown to the admin in-console to relay out-of-band — they are **not** emailed (the configmap comment claiming \"admin one-time codes\" relay over SMTP is aspirational; no code path does it).\n\nDeliverability foundation is genuinely in place: **DKIM (selector `knl1`), SPF, and DMARC are live in Cloudflare for `knllogistic.com`** via OCI Email Delivery with an approved sender (`configmap.yaml:49-55`). That covers the now-mandatory Gmail/Yahoo SPF+DKIM+DMARC+alignment bar for the current low send volume.\n\nEverything else a transactional-email system needs is **absent**:\n- **Plain-text only.** `otp_body` builds a `.body(...)` string — no HTML, no branding, no `multipart/alternative`. HTML-less is fine for spam scoring, but there is no branded template and no template system at all.\n- **No bounce/complaint handling, no suppression list.** No SNS/webhook ingest, nothing consuming OCI delivery events. This is the single biggest deliverability risk at scale: industry leaders treat an account-level suppression list as mandatory because re-sending to hard-bounced/complained addresses is read as spam-like and AWS SES will **put an account under review at ≥5% bounce / ≥0.1% complaint and pause sending at ≥10% bounce / ≥0.5% complaint** ([AWS SES enforcement FAQ](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ses/latest/dg/faqs-enforcement.html)). On open signup, an attacker can pump random addresses and drive your bounce rate up with no brake.\n- **No retry/queue.** `send_otp` is a synchronous in-request SMTP call; a transient relay failure becomes an immediate 502 (`auth-rest:804`). No backoff, no dead-letter, no idempotency key (AWS explicitly tells you to design idempotent sends — [SES deliverability](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ses/latest/dg/send-email-concepts-deliverability.html)).\n- **No rate-limiting at the email layer** (the signup *endpoint* is rate-limited, but the relay itself isn't, and SES/SendGrid both enforce per-second quotas with 429/`Retry-After` you'd need to honor — [SendGrid guide](https://www.captaindns.com/en/blog/sendgrid-transactional-email-technical-guide)).\n- **No deliverability monitoring** (no bounce/complaint rate dashboards or alarms).\n- **No per-event notifications.** Nothing emails on work-order assignment, approval-needed, SLA breach, inspection due, or evidence ready — all of which are standard for field-service/CMMS products ([Accruent](https://www.accruent.com/products/maintenance-connection/automated-notification), [ServiceNow SLA](https://www.servicenow.com/docs/bundle/xanadu-it-service-management/page/product/service-level-management/concept/c_SLANotifications.html)). Confirmed: `grep` over workorder/inspection/scheduling crates finds zero `EmailSender` usage.\n\nVerdict: **fit for its current job (relay a signup OTP) and resting on a correct DKIM/SPF/DMARC base, but not a production-grade transactional-email platform.** It cannot safely scale signup volume or carry business notifications.\n\n### MESSENGER — Strong, well-engineered core; production-ready as a basic auditable chat, but missing the feature set and the notification path users expect.\n\nWhat exists and is genuinely solid:\n- Threads (`work_order` / `team` / `dm` / `group`), messages, **read receipts** (coalesced per thread/user), keyset **pagination** with cursors, and **full-text search** (Postgres `tsvector` GIN + an ILIKE fallback for Korean — `adapter-postgres:466-504`).\n- **Evidence attachments** already tie into the #10 evidence pipeline (presign → upload → confirm → `messenger_message_attachments` → `evidence_media`).\n- **Realtime is real and well-built** (`platform/realtime/src/lib.rs`): WebSocket hub fed by Postgres `LISTEN/NOTIFY` carrying only IDs, with branch-scope + thread-membership authorization on fan-out, cursor-based **replay** on reconnect, and lagging-consumer back-pressure. Multi-tenant RLS is carefully armed in the background listener via an org stamped on the NOTIFY payload.\n- **Every mutation is audited** via `with_audit` (thread create, message send, read) — appropriate for the no-E2EE auditable design.\n- **Substantial test coverage** (~2,000 lines across adapter/rest/realtime/web).\n\nWhat's missing vs Slack/Teams/Intercom (all table-stakes per the benchmark — [Slack notifications](https://slack.com/help/articles/360025446073-Guide-to-Slack-notifications), [Intercom real-time](https://www.intercom.com/help/en/articles/258-real-time-messaging-explained)):\n- **No push/email notification on new messages.** This is the headline reliability gap (see (c)). Delivery is **live-WebSocket-only**: if the recipient isn't connected, the message produces zero notification — they see it only on the next manual reload. The platform already runs FCM/APNs/SMS push (`ProviderPushNotifier`, wired to dispatch + support in `app/src/lib.rs:1206,1220`), but messenger does **not** use it.\n- **No unread counts / badges** anywhere — confirmed absent in `messenger-state.ts`. Read receipts are stored but never aggregated into an unread count, so there's no per-thread or app badge.\n- **No edit / delete** — the schema has no `edited_at`/`deleted_at`, and there is no PATCH/DELETE on messages in OpenAPI. Standard in Slack/Teams.\n- **No presence, no typing indicators, no @mentions, no reactions, no replies/threading** — none exist in schema, API, or UI.\n- **Membership is fixed at thread creation** — no add/remove/leave member endpoints.\n- **Attachments are work-order-only** — the UI guards `uploadWorkOrderAttachment` behind `thread.work_order_id`, so DM/group/team threads can't attach media (the presign path requires a work order).\n- **Infinite scroll** is \"Load older\" button paging, not auto-scroll (minor).\n- **No message retention policy / compliance export.** Messages are audited individually but there's no eDiscovery-style export of conversations (Slack Discovery API / Teams Purview are the benchmark — [Slack Discovery](https://slack.com/help/articles/360002079527-A-guide-to-Slacks-Discovery-APIs)). For an explicitly auditable system this is a notable omission.\n\nVerdict: **the messaging *engine* is production-ready and better-architected than most in-house chat; the *product* is an MVP** — usable only while a user is actively watching the panel, and missing the everyday affordances (unread badges, mentions, edit/delete, reactions) that make chat feel complete.\n\n---\n\n## (b) Prioritized gap-closing backlog (high-value / low-effort first)\n\n### P0 — correctness/reliability, do first\n1. **Notify on new messages via existing push + email (messenger).** Highest value, moderate effort — the infra already exists. In `PostgresMessageNotifier`/the realtime hub or a new post-commit listener, for each thread member who is **not** currently connected and is behind on `messenger_read_receipts`, fan out an FCM/APNs/SMS push (reuse `state.push_notifier`) and/or an email. Mirror Slack's \"notify me when mentioned/DM'd and away\" ([Slack configure notifications](https://slack.com/help/articles/201355156-Configure-your-Slack-notifications)). *Needs:* a notion of online presence (the hub already knows live connections) + per-user notification prefs table. Files: `backend/crates/platform/realtime/src/lib.rs`, `backend/crates/messenger/adapter-postgres/src/lib.rs`, `backend/app/src/lib.rs:1176`.\n2. **Email bounce/complaint ingest + account-level suppression list (email).** Wire OCI Email Delivery's bounce/complaint feedback (or move to a provider with webhooks) into a `email_suppressions` table; check it before every send; never re-send to a suppressed address. This is the one mandatory guardrail keeping bounce/complaint rates under the SES-style review/pause envelope (≥5%/≥10% bounce, ≥0.1%/≥0.5% complaint — [AWS SES enforcement FAQ](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ses/latest/dg/faqs-enforcement.html)). Especially important because **signup is unauthenticated and open**. *Needs:* a migration, an ingest endpoint, suppression check in `email/src/lib.rs` send path.\n3. **Don't orphan accounts on email failure (email, small).** `signup` (`auth-rest:791-806`) creates the MEMBER account + mints the OTP, then sends email; a 502 on send leaves an undeliverable account behind. Either send before committing the account, or schedule cleanup of never-redeemed signup accounts. Low effort, prevents account-table litter from bounce storms.\n\n### P1 — high-value parity, moderate effort\n4. **Unread counts + badges (messenger).** Derive from `messenger_read_receipts` vs latest `messenger_messages` per thread; expose on the thread-list query (`adapter-postgres list_threads`) and render a badge in `MessengerPanel.tsx` + an app-level total. Low-moderate effort, big UX win.\n5. **Edit / delete messages (messenger).** Add `edited_at` + `deleted_at` (soft delete to preserve audit) columns (new migration), PATCH/DELETE routes (`messenger/rest`), audit each, and tombstone rendering in the UI. Soft delete keeps it auditable.\n6. **@mentions (messenger).** Parse `@user`, store mention rows, and route a targeted notification (ties into P0 #1). Files: domain (parse), adapter (persist), realtime/push (target).\n7. **Branded HTML email template with text fallback (email).** Add a `multipart/alternative` (HTML + the existing text) builder so OTP mail is branded; `multipart/alternative` is the deliverability-safe standard ([Mailtrap](https://mailtrap.io/blog/html-vs-plain-text-email/)). Modest effort in `email/src/lib.rs` (`lettre` supports it natively).\n\n### P2 — completeness / scale\n8. **Send queue + retry + idempotency (email).** Move sends off the request path into a worker with exponential backoff, a dead-letter, and an idempotency key per logical send ([AWS SES idempotency](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ses/latest/dg/send-email-concepts-deliverability.html)). Lets email carry P3 business notifications safely.\n9. **Per-event business email/push (workorder/inspection).** WO assigned, approval needed, SLA breach, inspection due, evidence ready — standard CMMS notifications ([Accruent](https://www.accruent.com/products/maintenance-connection/automated-notification)). Depends on #8 (queue) and per-user prefs.\n10. **Reactions, replies/threading, typing/presence indicators (messenger).** Standard chat affordances; presence can build on the hub's live-connection registry.\n11. **Mutable membership + non-WO attachments (messenger).** Add/remove/leave endpoints; generalize the attachment presign so DM/group/team threads can attach evidence too.\n12. **Deliverability monitoring + compliance export (email/messenger).** Bounce/complaint-rate dashboards + alarms (early warning before review/pause); and a conversation eDiscovery export for the messenger, fitting the auditable mandate ([Slack Discovery](https://slack.com/help/articles/360002079527-A-guide-to-Slacks-Discovery-APIs)).\n\n---\n\n## (c) Correctness / reliability risks live today\n1. **Messages can go unseen — no notification path (highest risk).** New-message delivery is live-WebSocket-only; an offline recipient gets nothing (no push, no email, no unread badge), so for an operational maintenance tool, time-sensitive coordination messages are silently missed until the user happens to reload. The push infra exists but isn't wired to messenger. → Backlog P0 #1, P1 #4.\n2. **No email suppression on an open, unauthenticated signup endpoint.** Repeated/abusive signups to bad addresses drive bounces/complaints with no brake; at provider scale this gets sending **paused** (≥10% bounce / ≥0.5% complaint per [AWS SES](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/ses/latest/dg/faqs-enforcement.html)). → P0 #2.\n3. **Synchronous in-request email send with no retry.** A transient OCI relay blip turns a legitimate signup into a hard 502; the account+code exist but the code never arrives, and there's no retry/queue. → P0 #3 / P2 #8.\n4. **Orphaned MEMBER accounts on email failure.** Account is created before the email succeeds; on send failure it's left behind unusable. → P0 #3.\n\nOne thing that is **not** a risk: message-send errors are surfaced (`auth-rest` returns 502 on email failure; messenger `send_message` returns the error to the client and the UI shows `sendFailed`) and realtime notify failures are logged, not silently swallowed in a way that loses the persisted message — Postgres remains source of truth and the message is committed before fan-out. The failure mode is missed *notification*, not lost *data*."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"stop_details":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2,"cache_creation_input_tokens":468,"cache_read_input_tokens":117391,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":468,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"diagnostics":null},"requestId":"req_011CcLc55FTQMDtH8rxvKkkF","attributionAgent":"general-purpose","type":"assistant","uuid":"e51319f3-fbaf-4f4f-8fac-25c9ea65bd7b","timestamp":"2026-06-23T17:44:25.200Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/jasonlee/Developer/maintenance","sessionId":"a4f6c1da-da69-4ccc-b409-be462b15706d","version":"2.1.185","gitBranch":"feat/multi-tenant-phase1","slug":"flickering-finding-valiant"}
